Special characters are used in some languages to represent pauses (known as "glottal stops"), and remembering them is essential for accurately representing a language's intonation patterns or stress.
There are two types of special characters used to represent pauses in different ways: one is for the glottal stop itself, and another is for representing a specific pause within a word or phrase.
The second type is used in locations where an accidental insertion of the character occurs, for example when it happens at the beginning or end of a word, as well as after another vowel or consonant: and each one has its own special operation depending on that location.
These characters may be used to indicate the absence of a sound or pause, either at the beginning or end of words or phrases, but not after another vowel or consonant.
Other characters may be used to indicate the absence of sound or pause at the beginning or end of words, but not after another vowel or consonant; for example, they may replace 'p' in places where it is normally silent (e.g., after a short 'a'), or mark the absence of an initial letter or sound, as well as indicating the end of a word or phrase.
